<p><b>Céline Marie Claudette Dion</b>, <span style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Order_of_Canada" title="Order of Canada">CC</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Order_of_Quebec" title="National Order of Quebec">OQ</a></span> <small style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">ChLD</a></small> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="/iː/ long 'e' in 'seed'">iː</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="/ɒ/ short 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted" title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span></a></span><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> <small>French: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[selin djɔ̃]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:Fr-C%C3%A9line-Dion.oga" title="File:Fr-Céline-Dion.oga"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/Fr-C%C3%A9line-Dion.oga" title="Fr-Céline-Dion.oga">listen</a>)</small>; born 30 March 1968) is a Canadian singer, songwriter, entrepreneur and occasional actress. Born into a large family from <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne,_Quebec" title="Charlemagne, Quebec">Charlemagne, Quebec</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion emerged as a teen star in the French-speaking world after her manager and future husband <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Ang%C3%A9lil" title="René Angélil">René Angélil</a> mortgaged his home to finance her first record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jam_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jam-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1990, she released the English-language album <i><a href="/wiki/Unison_(Celine_Dion_album)" title="Unison (Celine Dion album)">Unison</a></i>, establishing herself as a viable pop artist in North America and other English-speaking areas of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Enc_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Enc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Dion first gained international recognition in the 1980s by winning both the 1982 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yamaha_(manufacturer)" title="Yamaha (manufacturer)">Yamaha</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Popular_Song_Festival" title="World Popular Song Festival">World Popular Song Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_1988" title="Eurovision Song Contest 1988">1988 Eurovision Song Contest</a> where she <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest_1988" title="Switzerland in the Eurovision Song Contest 1988">represented Switzerland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bliss_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bliss-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Following a series of French albums in the early 1980s, she signed on to <a href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment" title="Sony Music Entertainment">CBS Records Canada</a> in 1986. During the 1990s, with the help of Angélil, she achieved worldwide fame after signing with <a href="/wiki/Epic_Records" title="Epic Records">Epic Records</a> and releasing several English albums along with additional French albums, becoming one of the most successful artists in pop music history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chuck_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chuck-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNN_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNNN-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> However, in 1999 at the height of her success, Dion announced a hiatus from entertainment in order to start a family and spend time with her husband, who had been diagnosed with cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNN_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNNN-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trans_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trans-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> She returned to the top of pop music in 2002 and signed a three-year (later extended to almost five years) contract to perform nightly in a five-star theatrical show at the Colosseum at <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Palace" title="Caesars Palace">Caesars Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paradise,_Nevada" title="Paradise, Nevada">Paradise, Nevada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lavid_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lavid-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Dion's music has been influenced by genres ranging from rock and <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">R&amp;B</a> to <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_classical_music" title="European classical music">classical</a>. Her recordings are mainly in French and English, although she also sings in Spanish, Italian, German, Latin, Japanese and Mandarin Chinese. While her releases have often received mixed critical reception, she is renowned for her technically skilled and powerful vocals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time1_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elysa_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elysa-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cove_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-cove-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion has won five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Falling_into_You" title="Falling into You">Falling Into You</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a> for "<a href="/wiki/My_Heart_Will_Go_On" title="My Heart Will Go On">My Heart Will Go On</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Celine_Dion_official_Grammy_source_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Celine_Dion_official_Grammy_source-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> She is the second best-selling female artist in the US during the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> era, with her albums <i>Falling Into You</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Talk_About_Love" title="Let's Talk About Love">Let's Talk About Love</a></i> both <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification#RIAA_Diamond_certifications" title="RIAA certification">certified Diamond</a> in the US,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, her 1995 album <i><a href="/wiki/D%27eux" title="D'eux">D'eux</a></i>, is the best-selling French-language album of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, after surpassing 175 million in album sales worldwide, she was presented with the Chopard Diamond Award at the <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a> for becoming the best-selling female artist of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion remains the best-selling Canadian artist in history and <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">one of the best-selling artists of all time</a> with record sales of more than 200 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1968.E2.80.931989:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings">1968–1989: Early life and career beginnings</span></h3>
<p>Dion was born in Charlemagne, Québec, Canada, the youngest of 14 children of <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9r%C3%A8se_Dion" title="Thérèse Dion">Thérèse</a> (née Tanguay), a homemaker, and Adhémar Dion, a butcher, both of French-Canadian descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion was raised a Roman Catholic in a poverty-stricken, but, by her own account, happy home in Charlemagne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNN_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-CNNN-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated12_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated12-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Music had always been a part of the family (Dion was named after the song <i>Céline</i>, recorded by French singer <a href="/wiki/Hugues_Aufray" title="Hugues Aufray">Hugues Aufray</a> two years before her birth <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>). On 13 August 1973, (at the age of five) the young Céline made her first public appearance at her brother Michel's wedding, where she performed <a href="/wiki/Christine_Charbonneau" title="Christine Charbonneau">Christine Charbonneau</a>'s song <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Du fil des aiguilles et du coton</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Thereafter, she continued to perform with her siblings in her parents' small <a href="/wiki/Piano_bar" title="Piano bar">piano bar</a> called <i>Le Vieux Baril</i>. From an early age Dion had dreamed of being a performer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time1_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Time1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> In a 1994 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People</a></i> magazine, she recalled, "I missed my family and my home, but I don't regret having lost my adolescence. I had one dream: I wanted to be a singer."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A9line_Dion_1986.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="196" data-file-width="100" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/C%C3%A9line_Dion_1986.jpg" width="100"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A9line_Dion_1986.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dion at the age of 18</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At age 12, Dion collaborated with her mother and her brother Jacques to compose her first song, "<a href="/wiki/Ce_n%27%C3%A9tait_qu%27un_r%C3%AAve" title="Ce n'était qu'un rêve">Ce n'était qu'un rêve</a>" ("It Was Only a Dream").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated12_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated12-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Her brother Michel Dondalinger Dion sent the recording to music manager René Angélil, whose name he discovered on the back of a <a href="/wiki/Ginette_Reno" title="Ginette Reno">Ginette Reno</a> album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jam_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jam-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Angélil was moved to tears by Dion's voice, and decided to make her a star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated12_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated12-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1981, he mortgaged his home to fund her first record, <i><a href="/wiki/La_voix_du_bon_Dieu" title="La voix du bon Dieu">La voix du bon Dieu</a></i> ("The Voice of the Good God"), which later became a local number-one hit and made Dion an instant star in Quebec. Her popularity spread to other parts of the world when she competed in the 1982 Yamaha World Popular Song Festival in Tokyo, Japan, and won the musician's award for "Top Performer" as well as the gold medal for "Best Song" with "<a href="/wiki/Tellement_j%27ai_d%27amour_pour_toi" title="Tellement j'ai d'amour pour toi">Tellement j'ai d'amour pour toi</a>" ("I Have So Much Love for You").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jam_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jam-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By 1983, in addition to becoming the first Canadian artist to receive a gold record in France for the single "<a href="/wiki/D%27amour_ou_d%27amiti%C3%A9" title="D'amour ou d'amitié">D'amour ou d'amitié</a>" ("Of Love or of Friendship"), Dion had also won several <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Award" title="Félix Award">Félix Awards</a>, including "Best Female performer" and "Discovery of the Year".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jam_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-Jam-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated20_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated20-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Further success in Europe, Asia, and Australia came when Dion represented <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Switzerland in the Eurovision Song Contest">Switzerland</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1988_Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="1988 Eurovision Song Contest">1988 Eurovision Song Contest</a> with the song <i><a href="/wiki/Ne_partez_pas_sans_moi" title="Ne partez pas sans moi">Ne partez pas sans moi</a></i> (<i>Don't Leave Without Me</i>) and won the contest by a close margin in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>, Ireland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> However, American success was yet to come as she was at that point exclusively a Francophone artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated18_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated18-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> At eighteen, after seeing a <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> performance, Dion told Angélil that she wanted to be a star like Jackson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Though confident in her talent, Angélil realized that her image needed to be changed in order for her to be marketed worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated12_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated12-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion receded from the spotlight for a number of months, during which she underwent dental surgery to improve her appearance, and was sent to the <a href="/wiki/Berlitz_Corporation" title="Berlitz Corporation">École Berlitz</a> in 1989 to polish her English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Enc_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Enc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1989, during a concert on the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Incognito_Tour" title="Incognito Tour">Incognito Tour</a></i>, Dion injured her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vocal_chords" title="Vocal chords">voice</a>. She consulted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otolaryngology" title="Otolaryngology">otorhinolaryngologist</a> William Gould,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bombardier_2009_172.E2.80.93173_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bombardier_2009_172.E2.80.93173-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Germain_p._279-280_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Germain_p._279-280-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> who gave her an ultimatum: have immediate surgery on her vocal cords, or do not utilize them at all for three weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bombardier_2009_172.E2.80.93173_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bombardier_2009_172.E2.80.93173-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion chose the latter and underwent vocal training with William Riley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bombardier_2009_172.E2.80.93173_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-Bombardier_2009_172.E2.80.93173-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bombardier_2009_172.E2.80.93173_40-3"><a href="#cite_note-Bombardier_2009_172.E2.80.93173-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Germain_p._279-280_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Germain_p._279-280-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Germain_p._279-280_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-Germain_p._279-280-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990.E2.80.9392:_Unison.2C_Dion_chante_Plamondon_and_Celine_Dion">1990–92: <i>Unison</i>, <i>Dion chante Plamondon</i> and <i>Celine Dion</i></span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div style="background:transparent;text-align:left;padding:2px">Dion's earlier English releases</div>
<div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:CelineDionWhereDoesMyHeartBeatNow.ogg" title="File:CelineDionWhereDoesMyHeartBeatNow.ogg">"Where Does My Heart Beat Now" (1990)</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="position:relative;display:block;width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="26.995623582766" data-mwprovider="local" data-mwtitle="CelineDionWhereDoesMyHeartBeatNow.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_0" poster="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.25wmf17/resources/assets/file-type-icons/fileicon-ogg.png" preload="none" style="width:220px"><source data-bandwidth="64782" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (65 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/64/CelineDionWhereDoesMyHeartBeatNow.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'></source>Sorry, your browser either has JavaScript disabled or does not have any supported player.<br/>

</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">"Where Does My Heart Beat Now", Dion's first North American hit, was 1980s soft rock. (Note the prominence of the electric guitar). It contrasts with the style of subsequent efforts.</div>
</div>

</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Two years after she learned English, Dion made her debut into the Anglophone market with <i><a href="/wiki/Unison_(Celine_Dion_album)" title="Unison (Celine Dion album)">Unison</a></i> (1990), the lead single having originally been recorded by <a href="/wiki/Laura_Branigan" title="Laura Branigan">Laura Branigan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jam_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-Jam-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> She incorporated the help of many established musicians, including Vito Luprano and Canadian producer <a href="/wiki/David_Foster" title="David Foster">David Foster</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time1_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Time1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was largely influenced by 1980s <a href="/wiki/Soft_rock" title="Soft rock">soft rock</a> music that quickly found a niche within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adult_contemporary" title="Adult contemporary">adult contemporary</a> radio format. <i>Unison</i> also hit the right notes with critics: Jim Faber of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> wrote that Dion's vocals were "tastefully unadorned", and that she never attempted to "bring off styles that are beyond her".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Stephen Erlewine of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">Allmusic</a></i> declared it as, "a fine, sophisticated American debut."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Singles from the album included "<a href="/wiki/(If_There_Was)_Any_Other_Way" title="(If There Was) Any Other Way">(If There Was) Any Other Way</a>", "<a href="/wiki/The_Last_to_Know" title="The Last to Know">The Last to Know</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Unison_(song)#C.C3.A9line_Dion_version" title="Unison (song)">Unison</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Where_Does_My_Heart_Beat_Now" title="Where Does My Heart Beat Now">Where Does My Heart Beat Now</a>", a mid-tempo soft-rock ballad which made prominent use of the electric guitar. The latter became her first single to reach the top-ten on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, peaking at number-four. The album established Dion as a rising singer in the United States, and across <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">Continental Europe</a> and Asia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 1991, Dion was a featured soloist in <i><a href="/wiki/Voices_That_Care" title="Voices That Care">Voices That Care</a></i>, a tribute to American troops fighting in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Desert_Storm" title="Operation Desert Storm">Operation Desert Storm</a>. Dion's real international breakthrough came when she duetted with <a href="/wiki/Peabo_Bryson" title="Peabo Bryson">Peabo Bryson</a> on the title track to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney" title="Disney">Disney</a>'s animated film <i><a href="/wiki/Beauty_and_the_Beast_(1991_film)" title="Beauty and the Beast (1991 film)">Beauty and the Beast</a></i> (1991).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated8_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated8-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The song captured a musical style that Dion would utilize in the future: sweeping, classically influenced ballads with soft instrumentation. Both a critical and commercial hit, the song became her second U.S. top-ten single, and won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Song</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Pop_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocal" title="Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocal">Best Pop Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time1_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-Time1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Beauty_and_the_Beast_(Disney_song)" title="Beauty and the Beast (Disney song)">Beauty and the Beast</a>" was featured on Dion's 1992 <a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion_(album)" title="Celine Dion (album)">self-titled album</a>, which, like her debut, had a strong pop rock influence combined with elements of soul and classical music. Owing to the success of the lead-off single and her collaborations with David Foster and <a href="/wiki/Diane_Warren" title="Diane Warren">Diane Warren</a>, the album was even more well-received commercially than <i>Unison</i>. Other singles that achieved moderate success included "<a href="/wiki/If_You_Asked_Me_To#C.C3.A9line_Dion_version" title="If You Asked Me To">If You Asked Me To</a>" (a <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">cover</a> of <a href="/wiki/Patti_LaBelle" title="Patti LaBelle">Patti LaBelle</a>'s song from the 1989 movie <i><a href="/wiki/Licence_to_Kill" title="Licence to Kill">Licence to Kill</a></i>) which peaked at number-four on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, the gospel-tinged "<a href="/wiki/Love_Can_Move_Mountains" title="Love Can Move Mountains">Love Can Move Mountains</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Nothing_Broken_but_My_Heart" title="Nothing Broken but My Heart">Nothing Broken but My Heart</a>".</p>
<p>Also during this time, Dion released the Francophone album <i><a href="/wiki/Dion_chante_Plamondon" title="Dion chante Plamondon">Dion chante Plamondon</a></i>. The album consisted mostly of covers, but featured 4 new songs: "<a href="/wiki/Des_mots_qui_sonnent_(song)" title="Des mots qui sonnent (song)">Des mots qui sonnent</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Je_danse_dans_ma_t%C3%AAte" title="Je danse dans ma tête">Je danse dans ma tête</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Quelqu%27un_que_j%27aime,_quelqu%27un_qui_m%27aime" title="Quelqu'un que j'aime, quelqu'un qui m'aime">Quelqu'un que j'aime, quelqu'un qui m'aime</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/L%27amour_existe_encore" title="L'amour existe encore">L'amour existe encore</a>". It was originally released in Canada and France during the 1991–1992 period, then later received an international release in 1994, the first French Celine Dion album to do so. "<a href="/wiki/Un_gar%C3%A7on_pas_comme_les_autres_(Ziggy)" title="Un garçon pas comme les autres (Ziggy)">Un garçon pas comme les autres (Ziggy)</a>" became a smash hit in France, reaching number-two and being certified gold. In Quebec, the album was certified Gold the day it was released.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>By 1992, <i>Unison</i>, <i>Céline Dion</i>, and numerous high-profile media appearances had propelled Dion to superstardom in North America. She had achieved one of her main objectives: wedging her way into the Anglophone market and achieving fame.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated18_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated18-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> However, while she was experiencing rising success in the U.S., her French fans in Canada criticized her for neglecting them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time1_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-Time1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated21_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated21-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> She would later rebuff these criticisms at the 1991 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Awards" title="Félix Awards">Félix Awards</a> show, where, after winning "English Artist of the Year", she openly refused to accept the award. She asserted that she was—and would always be—a French, not an English, artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Enc_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-Enc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Apart from her commercial success, there were also changes in Dion's personal life, as Angélil, who was twenty-six years her senior, transitioned from manager to lover. However, the relationship was kept a secret as they both feared that the public would find their relations inappropriate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated22_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated22-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1993.E2.80.9395:_The_Colour_of_My_Love_and_D.27eux">1993–95: <i>The Colour of My Love</i> and <i>D'eux</i></span></h3>
<p>In 1993, Dion announced her feelings for her manager by declaring him "the colour of [her] love" in the dedication section of her third English-language album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Colour_of_My_Love" title="The Colour of My Love">The Colour of My Love</a></i>. However, instead of criticizing their relationship as Dion had feared, fans embraced the couple.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time1_17-5"><a href="#cite_note-Time1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Eventually, Angélil and Dion married in an extravagant wedding ceremony in December 1994, which was broadcast live on Canadian television.</p>
<p>As with most of her catalog, <i>The Colour of my Love</i> had overriding themes of love and romance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated23_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated23-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> It became her most successful record up to that point, selling more than six million copies in the U.S., two million in Canada, and peaking at number-one in many countries. The album also spawned Dion's first U.S., Canadian, and Australian number-one single "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Power_of_Love_(Celine_Dion)" title="The Power of Love (Celine Dion)">The Power of Love</a>" (a remake of <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Rush" title="Jennifer Rush">Jennifer Rush</a>'s 1985 hit), which would become her <a href="/wiki/Signature_song" title="Signature song">signature hit</a> until she reached new career heights in the late 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated18_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated18-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The single "<a href="/wiki/When_I_Fall_in_Love#C.C3.A9line_Dion_and_Clive_Griffin_version" title="When I Fall in Love">When I Fall in Love</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Duet" title="Duet">duet</a> with <a href="/wiki/Clive_Griffin" title="Clive Griffin">Clive Griffin</a>, achieved moderate success on the U.S. and Canadian charts, and was nominated for two Grammy Awards, winning one. <i>The Colour of My Love</i> also became Dion's first major hit in Europe, particularly in the United Kingdom. Both the album and the single "<a href="/wiki/Think_Twice_(song)" title="Think Twice (song)">Think Twice</a>" simultaneously occupied the top of the British charts for five consecutive weeks. "Think Twice", which remained at number-one for seven weeks, eventually became the fourth single by a female artist to sell in excess of one million copies in the UK,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> while the album was eventually certified five-times platinum for two-million copies sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Dion kept to her French roots and continued to release many Francophone recordings between each English record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated15_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated15-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Generally, they achieved more credibility than her English-language works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated21_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated21-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> She released <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%80_l%27Olympia_(C%C3%A9line_Dion_album)" title="À l'Olympia (Céline Dion album)">À l'Olympia</a></i>, a live album that was recorded during one of Dion's concerts at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paris_Olympia" title="Paris Olympia">Paris Olympia</a> in 1994. It had one promotional single, a live version of "<a href="/wiki/Calling_You#C.C3.A9line_Dion_version" title="Calling You">Calling You</a>", which peaked at seventy-five on the French Singles Chart. She also recorded a bilingual version of <a href="/wiki/Petit_Papa_No%C3%ABl" title="Petit Papa Noël">Petit Papa Noël</a> with <a href="/wiki/Alvin_and_the_Chipmunks" title="Alvin and the Chipmunks">Alvin and the Chipmunks</a> for the 1994 holiday album <i><a href="/wiki/A_Very_Merry_Chipmunk" title="A Very Merry Chipmunk">A Very Merry Chipmunk</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/D%27eux" title="D'eux">D'eux</a></i> (also known as <i>The French Album</i> in the United States), was released in 1995, and it would go on to become the best-selling French-language album of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated15_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated15-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was mostly written and produced by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Goldman" title="Jean-Jacques Goldman">Jean-Jacques Goldman</a>, and amassed huge success with the singles "<a href="/wiki/Pour_que_tu_m%27aimes_encore" title="Pour que tu m'aimes encore">Pour que tu m'aimes encore</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Je_sais_pas" title="Je sais pas">Je sais pas</a>". "Pour que tu m'aimes encore" reached number 1 in France and stayed at the top position for twelve weeks. It was later certified Platinum in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The single also reached the top ten in the UK and Ireland, a rare accomplishment for a French song. The second single off the album, "Je sais pas", reached number-one on the French Singles Chart as well and was certified Silver there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> These songs would later become "If That's What It Takes" and "I Don't Know" on Dion's next English album, <i><a href="/wiki/Falling_into_You" title="Falling into You">Falling into You</a></i>.</p>
<p>During the mid-1990s and onward, Dion's albums were generally constructed on the basis of melodramatic Adult contemporary ballads, with sprinklings of up-tempo pop and rare forays into other genres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> She collaborated with many renowned writers and producers such as Jim Steinman and David Foster, who helped her to develop a signature sound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time1_17-6"><a href="#cite_note-Time1-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> While critical reviews fluctuated, Dion's releases performed increasingly well on the international charts, and in 1996 she won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Music_Award" title="World Music Award">World Music Award</a> for "World's Best-selling Female Recording Artist of the Year" for the third time. By the mid-1990s, she had established herself as one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling artists in the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inter_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Inter-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1996.E2.80.9399:_Falling_into_You.2C_Let.27s_Talk_About_Love_and_S.27il_suffisait_d.27aimer">1996–99: <i>Falling into You</i>, <i>Let's Talk About Love</i> and <i>S'il suffisait d'aimer</i></span></h3>

<p><i><a href="/wiki/Falling_into_You" title="Falling into You">Falling into You</a></i> (1996), Dion's fourth English-language album, presented the singer at the height of her popularity, and showed a further progression of her music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated22_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated22-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> In an attempt to reach a wider audience, the album combined many elements, such as complex orchestral sounds, African <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chanting" title="Chanting">chanting</a> and elaborate musical effects. Additionally, instruments like the violin, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_guitar" title="Spanish guitar">Spanish guitar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trombone" title="Trombone">trombone</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cavaquinho" title="Cavaquinho">cavaquinho</a> and saxophone created a new sound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated17_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated17-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The singles encompassed a variety of musical styles. The title track "<a href="/wiki/Falling_into_You_(song)" title="Falling into You (song)">Falling into You</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/River_Deep_%E2%80%93_Mountain_High" title="River Deep – Mountain High">River Deep – Mountain High</a>" (a <a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">Tina Turner</a> cover) made prominent use of percussion instruments; "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_All_Coming_Back_to_Me_Now#C.C3.A9line_Dion" title="It's All Coming Back to Me Now">It's All Coming Back to Me Now</a>" (produced by its writer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Steinman" title="Jim Steinman">Jim Steinman</a>) and a remake of <a href="/wiki/Eric_Carmen" title="Eric Carmen">Eric Carmen</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/All_by_Myself#C.C3.A9line_Dion_version" title="All by Myself">All by Myself</a>" maintained a soft-rock atmosphere, combined with the classical sound of the piano; and the number-one single "<a href="/wiki/Because_You_Loved_Me" title="Because You Loved Me">Because You Loved Me</a>", which was written by Diane Warren, was a pop ballad that served as the theme to the 1996 film <i><a href="/wiki/Up_Close_%26_Personal" title="Up Close &amp; Personal">Up Close &amp; Personal</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inter_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Inter-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Falling into You</i> garnered career-best reviews for Dion. While Dan Leroy wrote that it was not very different from her previous work,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> and Stephen Holden of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> and Natalie Nichols of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> wrote that the album was formulaic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> other critics, such as Chuck Eddy of <i>Entertainment Weekly</i>, Stephen Thomas Erlewine of <i>AMG</i> and Daniel Durchholz, lavished the album as "compelling", "passionate", "stylish", "elegant" and "remarkably well-crafted".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated17_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated17-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Falling Into You</i> became Dion's most critically and commercially successful album: it topped the charts in many countries and became one of the best-selling albums of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013, <a href="/wiki/CBC_Music" title="CBC Music">CBC Music</a> ranked <i>Falling into you</i> 33rd in their list of the 100 greatest Canadian albums ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> In the United States, the album reached number-one,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv.com_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtv.com-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> and was later certified 11x Platinum for over 11 million copies shipped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> In Canada, the album was certified diamond for over one million copies shipped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IFPI" title="IFPI">IFPI</a> certified <i>Falling into You</i> 9x Platinum, an accolade that has been given to only two other albums in history, with one of the two being Dion's own album, <i><a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Talk_About_Love" title="Let's Talk About Love">Let's Talk About Love</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The album also won <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Pop_Album" title="Best Pop Album">Best Pop Album</a>, and the academy's highest honor <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion's status on the world stage was further solidified when she was asked to perform "<a href="/wiki/The_Power_of_the_Dream" title="The Power of the Dream">The Power of the Dream</a>" at the opening ceremonies of the 1996 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta_Olympic_Games" title="Atlanta Olympic Games">Atlanta Olympic Games</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 1996, Dion launched the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falling_into_You_Tour" title="Falling into You Tour">Falling into You Tour</a> in support of her new album, giving concerts around the world for over a year.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Celine_Dion_Sept_2008_Long_Island_NY_with_dancers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Celine_Dion_Sept_2008_Long_Island_NY_with_dancers.jpg/220px-Celine_Dion_Sept_2008_Long_Island_NY_with_dancers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Celine_Dion_Sept_2008_Long_Island_NY_with_dancers.jpg/330px-Celine_Dion_Sept_2008_Long_Island_NY_with_dancers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Celine_Dion_Sept_2008_Long_Island_NY_with_dancers.jpg/440px-Celine_Dion_Sept_2008_Long_Island_NY_with_dancers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Celine_Dion_Sept_2008_Long_Island_NY_with_dancers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Céline Dion on stage with her dancers performing "<a href="/wiki/River_Deep_%E2%80%93_Mountain_High" title="River Deep – Mountain High">River Deep – Mountain High</a>" on the Taking Chances World Tour in September 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dion followed <i>Falling into You</i> with <i><a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Talk_About_Love" title="Let's Talk About Love">Let's Talk About Love</a></i> (1997), which was publicized as its sequel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated13_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated13-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> The recording process took place in London, New York City, and Los Angeles, and featured a host of special guests, such as <a href="/wiki/Barbra_Streisand" title="Barbra Streisand">Barbra Streisand</a> on "<a href="/wiki/Tell_Him_(Barbra_Streisand_and_Celine_Dion_song)" title="Tell Him (Barbra Streisand and Celine Dion song)">Tell Him</a>"; the <a href="/wiki/Bee_Gees" title="Bee Gees">Bee Gees</a> on "<a href="/wiki/Immortality_(Celine_Dion_song)" title="Immortality (Celine Dion song)">Immortality</a>"; and world-renowned <a href="/wiki/Tenor" title="Tenor">tenor</a> <a href="/wiki/Luciano_Pavarotti" title="Luciano Pavarotti">Luciano Pavarotti</a> on "<a href="/wiki/I_Hate_You_Then_I_Love_You" title="I Hate You Then I Love You">I Hate You Then I Love You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated22_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated22-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archives_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-archives-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Other musicians included <a href="/wiki/Carole_King" title="Carole King">Carole King</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">Sir George Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Adams" title="Bryan Adams">Bryan Adams</a> and Jamaican singer <a href="/wiki/Diana_King" title="Diana King">Diana King</a>, who added a <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> tinge to "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treat_Her_Like_a_Lady_(Celine_Dion_song)" title="Treat Her Like a Lady (Celine Dion song)">Treat Her Like a Lady</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> As with <i>Falling into You</i>, <i>Let's Talk About Love</i> was a major success for Dion, reaching number-one all over the world, attaining platinum status in twenty-four sales territories, and becoming the fastest selling album of her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> In the United States, the album topped the chart in its seventh week of release,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> and was later certified 10x Platinum in the U.S. for over 10 million copies shipped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> In Canada, the album sold 230,212 copies in its first week of release, which became, and still is, a record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> It was eventually certified diamond in Canada for over 1 million copies shipped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The most successful single from the album was the <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classically</a> influenced ballad "<a href="/wiki/My_Heart_Will_Go_On" title="My Heart Will Go On">My Heart Will Go On</a>", which was written and composed by <a href="/wiki/James_Horner" title="James Horner">James Horner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Will_Jennings" title="Will Jennings">Will Jennings</a>, and produced by Horner and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Afanasieff" title="Walter Afanasieff">Walter Afanasieff</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Serving as the love theme for the 1997 blockbuster film <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>, the song topped the charts across the world, and became Dion's <a href="/wiki/Signature_song" title="Signature song">signature song</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated19_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated19-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as winning the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a> for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The song also garnered Dion two Grammy Awards for "<a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a>" and the most coveted "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Record_of_the_Year" title="Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a>", (the song itself won four awards, but two were presented to the songwriters).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> "My Heart Will Go On" and "Think Twice" made her the only female artist in the UK to have two singles to sell more than a million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jealous_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-jealous-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> In support of her album, Dion embarked on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Let%27s_Talk_About_Love_Tour" title="Let's Talk About Love Tour">Let's Talk About Love Tour</a> between 1998 and 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Dion ended the 1990s with three more extremely successful albums: the <a href="/wiki/Christmas_music" title="Christmas music">Christmas album</a> <i><a href="/wiki/These_Are_Special_Times" title="These Are Special Times">These Are Special Times</a></i> (1998), the French-language album, <i><a href="/wiki/S%27il_suffisait_d%27aimer" title="S'il suffisait d'aimer">S'il suffisait d'aimer</a></i>, and the compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/All_the_Way..._A_Decade_of_Song" title="All the Way... A Decade of Song">All the Way... A Decade of Song</a></i> (1999).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> On <i>These Are Special Times</i>, Dion co-wrote the song "Don't Save It All For Christmas Day" along with <a href="/wiki/Ric_Wake" title="Ric Wake">Ric Wake</a> and Peter Zizzo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was her most classically influenced yet, with orchestral arrangements found on virtually every track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The album featured the single "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Your_Angel" title="I'm Your Angel">I'm Your Angel</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Duet" title="Duet">duet</a> with <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a>, which became Dion's fourth U.S. number one single, and a smash hit across the world. <i>All the Way... A Decade of Song</i> drew together her most successful hits coupled with seven new songs, including the lead off single "<a href="/wiki/That%27s_the_Way_It_Is_(Celine_Dion_song)" title="That's the Way It Is (Celine Dion song)">That's the Way It Is</a>", a cover of <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Flack" title="Roberta Flack">Roberta Flack</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/The_First_Time_Ever_I_Saw_Your_Face" title="The First Time Ever I Saw Your Face">The First Time Ever I Saw Your Face</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/All_the_Way_(Frank_Sinatra_song)" title="All the Way (Frank Sinatra song)">All the Way</a>", a duet with <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>All the way</i> became one of the best-selling compilation albums of all time, reaching number-one in the United States for three weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv.com_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-mtv.com-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was later certified 7x Platinum in the U.S. for 7 million copies shipped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> It also topped the charts in the UK,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Canada,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jam.21_Showbiz_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jam.21_Showbiz-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> and Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Her last French-language studio album of the 1990s, <i>S'il suffisait d'aimer</i>, was very successful as well, topping the charts in every major French-speaking country, including France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Switzerland,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> Belgium Wallonia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> and Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jam.21_Showbiz_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jam.21_Showbiz-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> In France, the album was certified diamond, selling 1.5 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of the 1990s, Celine Dion had sold more than 100 million albums worldwide, and had won a slew of industry awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Her status as one of the music industry's biggest pop divas was further solidified when she was asked to perform on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s <i>Divas Live</i> special in 1998, with superstars <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha Franklin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Estefan" title="Gloria Estefan">Gloria Estefan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain" title="Shania Twain">Shania Twain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> That year she also received two of the highest honours from her home country: "Officer of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Canada" title="Order of Canada">Order of Canada</a> for Outstanding Contribution to the World of Contemporary Music"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg.ca_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-gg.ca-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gazette.gc.ca_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-gazette.gc.ca-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> and "Officer of the <a href="/wiki/National_Order_of_Quebec" title="National Order of Quebec">National Order of Quebec</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ordre-national.gouv.qc.ca_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-ordre-national.gouv.qc.ca-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> A year later she was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Broadcast_Hall_of_Fame" title="Canadian Broadcast Hall of Fame">Canadian Broadcast Hall of Fame</a>, and was honoured with a star on <a href="/wiki/Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame" title="Canada's Walk of Fame">Canada's Walk of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starting from the mid-nineties, the <a href="/wiki/Pop_rock" title="Pop rock">pop rock</a> influence that was more noticeable in her earlier releases, was replaced by a more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adult_contemporary" title="Adult contemporary">Adult contemporary</a> feel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated13_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated13-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, the recurring theme of "love" dominated most of her releases, which led to some critics dismissing her music as banal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated24_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated24-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Other critics, like Elysa Gardner and Jose F. Promis, praised her voice during this period, describing it as a "technical marvel".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Steve Dollar, in his review of <i>These Are Special Times</i>, opined that Dion was a "vocal Olympian for whom there ain't no mountain—or scale—high enough."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000.E2.80.9303:_Hiatus.2C_A_New_Day_Has_Come.2C_One_Heart_and_1_fille_.26_4_types">2000–03: Hiatus, <i>A New Day Has Come</i>, <i>One Heart</i> and <i>1 fille &amp; 4 types</i></span></h3>
<p>After releasing and promoting thirteen albums during the 1990s, Dion stated that she needed to settle down, and announced on her latest album <i><a href="/wiki/All_the_Way..._A_Decade_of_Song" title="All the Way... A Decade of Song">All the Way... A Decade of Song</a></i>, that she needed to take a step back from the spotlight and enjoy life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNN_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-CNNN-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vh1_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-vh1-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Angélil's diagnosis with <a href="/wiki/Esophageal_cancer" title="Esophageal cancer">throat cancer</a> also prompted her to hiatus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> While on break, Dion was unable to escape the spotlight. In 2000, the <i><a href="/wiki/National_Enquirer" title="National Enquirer">National Enquirer</a></i> published a false story about the singer. Brandishing a picture of Dion and her husband, the magazine misquoted Dion, printing the headline, "Celine — 'I'm Pregnant With Twins!'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion later sued the magazine for more than twenty million dollars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The editors of the <i>Enquirer</i> printed an apology and a full retraction to Dion in the next issue, and donated money to the <a href="/wiki/American_Cancer_Society" title="American Cancer Society">American Cancer Society</a> in honor of Dion and her husband. A year after the incident, after undergoing fertility treatments, Dion gave birth to a son, René-Charles Dion Angélil, on 25 January 2001, in Florida.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, Dion returned to the music scene, and in a televised performance sang "<a href="/wiki/God_Bless_America#Celine_Dion" title="God Bless America">God Bless America</a>" at the benefit concert <a href="/wiki/America:_A_Tribute_to_Heroes" title="America: A Tribute to Heroes">America: A Tribute to Heroes</a>. Chuck Taylor of <i>Billboard</i> wrote, "the performance... brings to mind what has made her one of the celebrated vocalists of our time: the ability to render emotion that shakes the soul. Affecting, meaningful, and filled with grace, this is a musical reflection to share with all of us still searching for ways to cope."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion would perform it again in 2003 during pregame festivities for <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXVII" title="Super Bowl XXXVII">Super Bowl XXXVII</a> in <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm_Stadium" title="Qualcomm Stadium">San Diego</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2001, Dion published her autobiography, <i>My Story, My Dream</i> which chronicled her rags to riches story.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Dion ended her three-year sabbatical from the music industry with the aptly titled album <i><a href="/wiki/A_New_Day_Has_Come" title="A New Day Has Come">A New Day Has Come</a></i>, released in March 2002. The album was Dion's most personal yet, with songs focusing on her motherhood and maturation as a woman such as "<a href="/wiki/A_New_Day_Has_Come_(song)" title="A New Day Has Come (song)">A New Day Has Come</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Goodbye%27s_(The_Saddest_Word)" title="Goodbye's (The Saddest Word)">Goodbye's (The Saddest Word)</a>". She stated: "becoming a mother makes you a grown-up."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vh1_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-vh1-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> She stated, "<i>A New Day Has Come</i>, for Rene, for me, is the baby. It has everything to do with the baby...That song "A New Day Has Come" represents very well the mood I'm feeling right now. It represents the whole album."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>A New Day Has Come</i> debuted at number one in over 17 countries, including the United Kingdom and Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> In the United States, the album debuted at number one on the Billboard 200, with first week sales of 527,000 copies; marking her first number one debut on the chart, as well as the highest debut sales week of her career in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> It was eventually certified 3x Platinum in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> and 6x Platinum in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A9line_Dion-AFR.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="283" data-file-width="322" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/C%C3%A9line_Dion-AFR.JPG/220px-C%C3%A9line_Dion-AFR.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ee/C%C3%A9line_Dion-AFR.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ee/C%C3%A9line_Dion-AFR.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A9line_Dion-AFR.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dion performing "<a href="/wiki/God_Bless_America" title="God Bless America">God Bless America</a>" with members of the Band of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force_Reserve" title="U.S. Air Force Reserve">U.S. Air Force Reserve</a>, 2002.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While the album was commercially successful, critical reviews suggested that it was "forgettable" and the lyrics were "lifeless".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Both Rob Sheffield of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine, and Ken Tucker of <i>Entertainment Weekly</i>, stated that Dion's music had not developed much during her break, and classed her material as trite and mediocre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Sal Cinquemani of <i><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant</a></i> magazine called the album "a lengthy collection of drippy, gooey pop fluffer-nutter."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The first single off the album, <i><a href="/wiki/A_New_Day_Has_Come_(song)" title="A New Day Has Come (song)">A New Day Has Come</a></i> peaked at No.22 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> charts, being an airplay-only release. On the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Adult_Contemporary_Tracks" title="Hot Adult Contemporary Tracks">Hot Adult Contemporary Tracks</a>, however the song spent 21 consecutive weeks at number 1, breaking the record for the longest span at the top.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> The previous record holders were <a href="/wiki/Phil_Collins" title="Phil Collins">Phil Collins</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/You%27ll_Be_in_My_Heart" title="You'll Be in My Heart">You'll Be in My Heart</a></i> and Dion's own <i><a href="/wiki/Because_You_Loved_Me" title="Because You Loved Me">Because You Loved Me</a>,</i> both of which lasted nineteen weeks at number 1. During 2002, she performed for many benefit concerts, including her second appearance on VH1 Divas Live, a concert to benefit the VH1 Save The Music Foundation, alongside <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anastacia" title="Anastacia">Anastacia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dixie_Chicks" title="Dixie Chicks">Dixie Chicks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyndi_Lauper" title="Cyndi Lauper">Cyndi Lauper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Nicks" title="Stevie Nicks">Stevie Nicks</a>.</p>
<p>In conjunction with an endorsement deal with <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a>, Dion released <i><a href="/wiki/One_Heart" title="One Heart">One Heart</a></i> (2003), an album that represented her appreciation for life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> The album largely consisted of pop and dance music—a deviation from the soaring, melodramatic ballads, for which she had been known. Although the album achieved moderate success, <i>One Heart</i> was met with mixed criticism, and words such as "predictable" and "banal" appeared even in the most lenient reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-One_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-One-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> A cover of the 1989 Cyndi Lauper hit "<a href="/wiki/I_Drove_All_Night#C.C3.A9line_Dion_version" title="I Drove All Night">I Drove All Night</a>", released to launch her advertising campaign with <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> incorporated elements of dance-pop and rock and roll. The advertising deal was met with criticism, with some stating that Dion was trying to cater to her sponsors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> However, people like Bonita Stewart, who was the director of Chrysler Group Marketing Communications stated that "Chrysler was taken by how her appeal crossed ethnic lines." She also added, "She brings sophistication, refinement, romance and passion to the brand."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After <i>One Heart</i>, Dion released her next English Language studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Miracle_(Celine_Dion_album)" title="Miracle (Celine Dion album)">Miracle</a></i> (2004). <i>Miracle</i> was a multimedia project conceived by Dion and Australian photographer <a href="/wiki/Anne_Geddes" title="Anne Geddes">Anne Geddes</a>, and had a theme centering on babies and motherhood. The album was filled with lullabies and other songs of maternal love and inspiration, including covers of <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armstrong" title="Louis Armstrong">Louis Armstrong</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/What_a_Wonderful_World" title="What a Wonderful World">What a Wonderful World</a>" and <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Boy_(Darling_Boy)#C.C3.A9line_Dion_version" title="Beautiful Boy (Darling Boy)">Beautiful Boy</a>". The reviews for <i>Miracle</i> were mixed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celebr_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-celebr-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> Stephen Thomas Erlewine of Allmusic.com gave the album three of out five stars, stating, "The worst you can say about the record is that there are no surprises, but the audience for this record doesn't want surprises; they want comfort, whether it arrives in polished music or artsy photos of newborns, and Miracle provides both, which makes it appealing for those expectant or new mothers in Dion's audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celebr_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-celebr-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chuck_Taylor_(Billboard_writer_and_editor)" title="Chuck Taylor (Billboard writer and editor)">Chuck Taylor</a> of <i>Billboard</i> magazine wrote that the single "Beautiful Boy" was "an unexpected gem" and called Dion "a timeless, enormously versatile artist",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> Chuck Arnold of <i>People</i> Magazine, however, labeled the album as excessively sentimental,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> while Nancy Miller of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> opined that "the whole earth-mama act is just opportunism, reborn".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Miracle</i> debuted at number four on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart and number one in Canada, and was eventually certified platinum by the RIAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Francophone album <i><a href="/wiki/1_fille_%26_4_types" title="1 fille &amp; 4 types">1 fille &amp; 4 types</a></i> (<i>1 Girl &amp; 4 Guys</i>), released in October 2003, fared better than her previous two releases, and showed Dion trying to distance herself from the "diva" image. She recruited <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Goldman" title="Jean-Jacques Goldman">Jean-Jacques Goldman</a>, Gildas Arzel, Eric Benzi, and Jacques Veneruso, with whom she had previously worked on two of her best-selling French albums <i><a href="/wiki/S%27il_suffisait_d%27aimer" title="S'il suffisait d'aimer">S'il suffisait d'aimer</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/D%27eux" title="D'eux">D'eux</a></i>. Labeled "the album of pleasure" by Dion herself, the album cover showed Dion in a simple and relaxed manner, contrary to the choreographed poses usually found on her album covers. The album achieved widespread commercial success in France, Canada, and Belgium where it reached number one. In France, the album debuted at number one and was later certified 2x platinum after selling over 700,000 copies. Critic, Stephen Erlewine of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">Allmusic</a></i> wrote that Dion's vocals "are back at top of their game" and that she was "getting back to pop basics and performing at a level unheard in a while."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Though her albums were commercially successful, they did not achieve the sales or the reception of her previous works. Her songs received less airplay as radio became less embracing of balladeers like Dion, Carey, and Houston, and was focused on more up-tempo, <a href="/wiki/Urban_contemporary" title="Urban contemporary">Urban</a>/<a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">Hip-hop</a> songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> Regardless, by 2004, Dion had accumulated sales of more than 175 million albums worldwide, and received the Chopard Diamond Award from the World Music Awards for her achievements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the official World Music Awards website, the award is rare; it is "not presented every year" and an artist can only be presented with the award for selling "over 100 million albums during their career."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2003.E2.80.9307:_A_New_Day_.E2.80.A6">2003–07: <i>A New Day …</i></span></h3>
<p>In early 2002, Dion had announced a three-year, 600-show contract to appear five nights a week in an entertainment extravaganza, <i><a href="/wiki/A_New_Day..." title="A New Day...">A New Day...</a></i>, at <a href="/wiki/The_Colosseum_at_Caesars_Palace" title="The Colosseum at Caesars Palace">The Colosseum at Caesars Palace</a>, Las Vegas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lavid_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lavid-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> This move was generally seen as risky, but journalist Miriam Nunzio wrote that it was "one of the smartest business decisions in years by any major recording artist".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion conceived the idea for the show after seeing <i><a href="/wiki/O_(Cirque_du_Soleil)" title="O (Cirque du Soleil)">O</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Franco_Dragone" title="Franco Dragone">Franco Dragone</a> during her break from recording, and it premiered on 25 March 2003, in a 4,000-seat arena specifically designed for her show and modeled after the Roman Colosseum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lavid_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lavid-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Many stars attended the opening night including <a href="/wiki/Dick_Clark" title="Dick Clark">Dick Clark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Thicke" title="Alan Thicke">Alan Thicke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kathy_Griffin" title="Kathy Griffin">Kathy Griffin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lance_Bass" title="Lance Bass">Lance Bass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>, who hosted the television special.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> The show, directed by Dragone and choreographed by the renowned <a href="/wiki/Mia_Michaels" title="Mia Michaels">Mia Michaels</a>, was a combination of dance, music, and visual effects. It included Dion performing her biggest hits against an array of dancers and special effects. Reviewer Mike Weatherford felt that, at first, Dion was not as relaxed as she should be, and at times, it was hard to find the singer among the excessive stage ornamentation and dancers. However, he noted that the show had become more enjoyable over the course of its run, due to Dion's improved stage-presence and simplified costumes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated19_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated19-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The show was well-received by audiences, despite the complaints of expensive tickets; it routinely sold out until its end in late 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> Ticket prices averaged $135.33.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/Pollstar" title="Pollstar">Pollstar</a></i>, Dion sold 322,000 tickets and grossed US$43.9 million in the first half of 2005, and by July 2005, she had sold out 315 out of 384 shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of 2005, Dion grossed more than US$76 million, placing sixth on <i>Billboard's Money Makers list for 2005</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>A New Day...</i> was the 6th biggest selling tour in America in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Because of the show's success, Dion's contract was extended into 2007 for an undisclosed sum. On 5 January 2007 it was announced that the show would end on 15 December 2007, with tickets for the period after October 2007 having gone on sale from 1 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> During its entire run, the show accumulated a total gross of $400 million, while being seen by nearly 3 million fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_in_Las_Vegas_-_A_New_Day..." title="Live in Las Vegas - A New Day...">Live in Las Vegas - A New Day...</a></i> DVD was released on 10 December 2007 in Europe and the following day in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007.E2.80.9310:_D.27elles.2C_Taking_Chances_and_Taking_Chances_Tour">2007–10: <i>D'elles</i>, <i>Taking Chances</i> and Taking Chances Tour</span></h3>
