<p>On 21 May 2007, Dion released the French-language album <i><a href="/wiki/D%27elles" title="D'elles">D'elles</a></i> <i>(About Them)</i>, which debuted at the top of the Canadian album charts, selling 72,200 copies in its first week. It marked her tenth number-one album in the SoundScan era, and her eighth to debut at the top position. In Canada, the album has been certified 2× platinum, and within the first month had already shipped half a million units worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>D'Elles</i> also reached No. 1 in France and Belgium. The first single "<a href="/wiki/Et_s%27il_n%27en_restait_qu%27une_(je_serais_celle-l%C3%A0)" title="Et s'il n'en restait qu'une (je serais celle-là)">Et s'il n'en restait qu'une (je serais celle-là)</a>" (meaning "And If There Was Only One Woman Left (I Would Be That One)") debuted at the top of the French singles chart a month earlier. Later that same year, Dion released the English album <i><a href="/wiki/Taking_Chances" title="Taking Chances">Taking Chances</a></i> on 12 November in Europe, and 13 November in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> Her first English studio album since 2003's <i>One Heart</i>, it featured pop, R&amp;B, and rock inspired music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> For this album, Dion collaborated with <a href="/wiki/John_Shanks" title="John Shanks">John Shanks</a> and ex-<a href="/wiki/Evanescence" title="Evanescence">Evanescence</a> guitarist <a href="/wiki/Ben_Moody" title="Ben Moody">Ben Moody</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Kristian_Lundin" title="Kristian Lundin">Kristian Lundin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peer_Astrom" title="Peer Astrom">Peer Astrom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linda_Perry" title="Linda Perry">Linda Perry</a>, Japanese singer <a href="/wiki/Yuna_Ito" title="Yuna Ito">Yuna Ito</a>, and R&amp;B singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Ne-Yo" title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion stated, "I think this album represents a positive evolution in my career ... I'm feeling strong, maybe a little gutsier than in the past, and just as passionate about music and life as I ever was."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion launched her year-long worldwide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taking_Chances_Tour" title="Taking Chances Tour">Taking Chances Tour</a> on 14 February 2008 in South Africa, performing 132 dates in stadiums and arenas across five continents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Celine_Dion_Concert_Singing_Taking_Chances_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1541" data-file-width="1171" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Celine_Dion_Concert_Singing_Taking_Chances_2008.jpg/170px-Celine_Dion_Concert_Singing_Taking_Chances_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Celine_Dion_Concert_Singing_Taking_Chances_2008.jpg/255px-Celine_Dion_Concert_Singing_Taking_Chances_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Celine_Dion_Concert_Singing_Taking_Chances_2008.jpg/340px-Celine_Dion_Concert_Singing_Taking_Chances_2008.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Celine_Dion_Concert_Singing_Taking_Chances_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dion during her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taking_Chances_Tour" title="Taking Chances Tour">Taking Chances Tour</a> concert in <a href="/wiki/Bell_Centre" title="Bell Centre">Bell Centre</a>, Montréal, on 19 August 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Taking Chances Tour was a great success in the United States, reaching the Number 1 spot on the <i>Billboard</i> Boxscore, having sold out every concert in the U.S. and Canada. In addition, she appeared on <a href="/wiki/Idol_Gives_Back" title="Idol Gives Back">Idol Gives Back</a> for a second year in a row. Dion was nominated for six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juno_Awards" title="Juno Awards">Juno Awards</a> in 2008, adding to her 53 previous nominations (an all-time record). Her nominations included Artist of the Year, Pop Album of the Year (for <i>Taking Chances</i>), Francophone Album of the Year (for <i>D'elles</i>) and Album of the Year (for both <i>Taking Chances</i> and <i>D'elles</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year, Dion was nominated for 3 Juno Awards including the Fan Choice Award, Song of the Year (for <i>Taking Chances</i>), and Music DVD of the Year (for <i>Live in Las Vegas — A New Day...</i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 August 2008, Dion presented a free outdoor concert, mostly in French<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reportage400e_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-reportage400e-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> on the <a href="/wiki/Plains_of_Abraham" title="Plains of Abraham">Plains of Abraham</a>, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qu%C3%A9bec_City" title="Québec City">Québec City</a>, Canada, for the 400th anniversary of Québec City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> The celebration gathered approximately 490,000 people. The concert, called <i><a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9line_sur_les_Plaines" title="Céline sur les Plaines">Céline sur les Plaines</a></i>, was released on DVD on 11 November 2008 in Québec and was released on 20 May 2009 in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> The end of October 2008 saw the worldwide release of a comprehensive English-language greatest hits album called <i><a href="/wiki/My_Love:_Essential_Collection" title="My Love: Essential Collection">My Love: Essential Collection</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2009, Celine Dion was named the 20th best-selling artist of the decade and the second-best-selling female artist of the decade in the United States, selling an estimated 17.57 million albums there since 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2009, <i>Forbes</i> reported that Dion earned $100 million during 2008. In December 2009, Pollstar announced that Dion was the best-selling solo touring act of the decade and the second-best-selling touring act of the decade, behind only the <a href="/wiki/Dave_Matthews_Band" title="Dave Matthews Band">Dave Matthews Band</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chicagotribune.com_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-chicagotribune.com-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion grossed $522.2 million during the decade, a large portion of that sum coming from her five-year residency at <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Palace" title="Caesars Palace">Caesars Palace</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chicagotribune.com_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-chicagotribune.com-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 February 2010 Dion released into theaters a documentary film about her <i>Taking Chances Tour</i>, titled, <i><a href="/wiki/Celine:_Through_the_Eyes_of_the_World" title="Celine: Through the Eyes of the World">Celine: Through the Eyes of the World</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday.com_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday.com-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> The documentary shows behind-the-scenes footage of Dion both onstage and offstage, along with footage of Dion with her family as they traveled the world with her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday.com_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday.com-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> The distributor is the <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Entertainment" title="Sony Pictures Entertainment">Sony Pictures</a> subsidiary, <a href="/wiki/Hot_Ticket" title="Hot Ticket">Hot Ticket</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday.com_167-2"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday.com-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was later released on Blu-ray and DVD on 4 May 2010, along with the CD/DVD, <i><a href="/wiki/Taking_Chances_World_Tour:_The_Concert" title="Taking Chances World Tour: The Concert">Taking Chances World Tour: The Concert</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_Grammy_Awards" title="2010 Grammy Awards">52nd Grammy Awards</a> in February 2010, Dion joined <a href="/wiki/Carrie_Underwood" title="Carrie Underwood">Carrie Underwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Hudson" title="Jennifer Hudson">Jennifer Hudson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smokey_Robinson" title="Smokey Robinson">Smokey Robinson</a> to perform the song "<a href="/wiki/Earth_Song" title="Earth Song">Earth Song</a>" during the 3-D <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> tribute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CelineDion_concert.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1607" data-file-width="2797" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/CelineDion_concert.jpg/220px-CelineDion_concert.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/CelineDion_concert.jpg/330px-CelineDion_concert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/CelineDion_concert.jpg/440px-CelineDion_concert.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CelineDion_concert.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Céline Dion on stage performing "<a href="/wiki/Eyes_on_Me_(Celine_Dion_song)" title="Eyes on Me (Celine Dion song)">Eyes On Me</a>" during her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taking_Chances_Tour" title="Taking Chances Tour">Taking Chances Tour</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montr%C3%A9al" title="Montréal">Montréal</a>, Canada in August 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In January 2010, <i>The <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> presented its annual list of the top ten largest earners of the year, revealing that Dion took the top spot for the entire decade, with <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$US</a>747.9 million in total revenue from 2000–2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> The largest haul came from ticket sales, totaling $522.2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, Dion was named "Artist of the Decade" in her native Canadian province of Québec, announced by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montr%C3%A9al" title="Montréal">Montréal</a>-based newspaper, <i>Le Journal de Québec</i> in 2009 December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lejournaldequebec.canoe.ca_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-lejournaldequebec.canoe.ca-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> A public <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Online_survey" title="Online survey">online survey</a> asked responders to vote for who they believe deserved the above-mentioned accolade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lejournaldequebec.canoe.ca_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-lejournaldequebec.canoe.ca-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Furthermore, in a May 2010 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harris_Poll" title="Harris Poll">Harris Poll</a>, Dion was named the most popular musician in the United States, ahead of <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, while factoring in gender, political affiliations, geographic region of residence, and income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> Specifically, Dion was the most popular musician in the female demographic, as well as among all Democrats, those who live in the eastern United States and southern United States, and those who have incomes between US$35k and US$74.9k.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2010, she released the single "<a href="/wiki/Voler" title="Voler">Voler</a>", a duet with French singer <a href="/wiki/Michel_Sardou" title="Michel Sardou">Michel Sardou</a>. The song was later included on Sardou's album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, it was announced in October 2010 that Dion wrote and composed a new song for Canadian singer, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Dupr%C3%A9" title="Marc Dupré">Marc Dupré</a> entitled "Entre deux mondes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.93present:_Celine.2C_Sans_attendre_and_Loved_Me_Back_to_Life">2011–present: <i>Celine</i>, <i>Sans attendre</i> and <i>Loved Me Back to Life</i></span></h3>
<p>In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People</a></i> magazine published in February 2010, Dion announced that she would be returning to Caesars Palace in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Celine_(residency_show)" title="Celine (residency show)">Celine</a></i>, a three-year residency for seventy shows a year, beginning 15 March 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-people1_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-people1-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> She stated that the show will feature, "all the songs from my repertoire that people want to hear" and will contain a selection of music from classic Hollywood films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-people1_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-people1-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> To promote her return to Las Vegas, Dion made an appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oprah_Winfrey_Show" title="The Oprah Winfrey Show">The Oprah Winfrey Show</a></i> on 21 February, during the show's final season, marking her record twenty-seventh appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, for a record sixth time, Dion performed at the <a href="/wiki/83rd_Academy_Awards" title="83rd Academy Awards">83rd Academy Awards</a>, where she sang the song "Smile," as part of the ceremony's "In Memoriam" segment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> On 4 September, Dion appeared on the 2011 MDA Labor Telethon Event and presented a prerecorded performance of "<a href="/wiki/Open_Arms_(Journey_song)" title="Open Arms (Journey song)">Open Arms</a>" from her new Las Vegas show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> On 1 October 2011, the OWN Network premiered a documentary on Dion's life, detailing the months before, during and after her pregnancy, to the makings of her new Las Vegas Show, called, "Celine: 3 Boys and a New Show".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> The documentary became the second highest rated show on TV OWN Canada. In October, <a href="/wiki/FlightNetwork" title="FlightNetwork">FlightNetwork</a>.com conducted a poll asking 780 participants which celebrity they would most like to sit next to on an airplane. Dion was the top favorite, with 23.7% of the vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, in September, Dion released the 14th perfume from her <a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion_Parfums" title="Celine Dion Parfums">Celine Dion Parfums</a> Collection, called "Signature".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celinedion1_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-celinedion1-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> On 15 September, Dion made an appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Concerto:_One_Night_in_Central_Park" title="Concerto: One Night in Central Park">free concert</a> of world-famous tenor, <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Bocelli" title="Andrea Bocelli">Andrea Bocelli</a>, in Central Park in New York.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012 she performed at the 16th Jazz and Blues Festival in <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2012, Sony Music Entertainment released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Best_of_Celine_Dion_%26_David_Foster" title="The Best of Celine Dion &amp; David Foster">The Best of Celine Dion &amp; David Foster</a></i> in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion began recording songs for her next English and French albums during April and May 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cd1_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-cd1-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> The French-language album, <i><a href="/wiki/Sans_attendre" title="Sans attendre">Sans attendre</a></i> was released on 2 November 2012 and was a smash success in all French-speaking territories, especially in France where it achieved diamond status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> The English-language album was postponed to 1 November 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> Titled <i><a href="/wiki/Loved_Me_Back_to_Life" title="Loved Me Back to Life">Loved Me Back to Life</a></i>, it included collaborations with an exceptional team of songwriters and producers, including duets with <a href="/wiki/Ne-Yo" title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> The lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Loved_Me_Back_to_Life_(song)" title="Loved Me Back to Life (song)">Loved Me Back to Life</a>" was released on 3 September 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Sans_attendre_Tour" title="Sans attendre Tour">Sans attendre Tour</a> in November 2013 and performed in Belgium and France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breakaway_(Celine_Dion_song)" title="Breakaway (Celine Dion song)">Breakaway</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Incredible_(Celine_Dion_and_Ne-Yo_song)" title="Incredible (Celine Dion and Ne-Yo song)">Incredible</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Water_and_a_Flame#Celine_Dion_version" title="Water and a Flame">Water and a Flame</a>" were chosen as next singles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video for "Incredible" was uploaded onto Dion's official <a href="/wiki/Vevo" title="Vevo">Vevo</a> channel in early June 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 May 2014, Dion released a three-disc set (2CD/DVD and 2CD/Blu-ray) titled <i><a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9line_une_seule_fois_/_Live_2013" title="Céline une seule fois / Live 2013">Céline une seule fois / Live 2013</a></i>, which reached top ten on the album charts in France, Canada and Belgium Wallonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="CelineDion.com is not an independent source (May 2014)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On 13 August 2014, Dion announced the indefinite postponement of all her show business activities, including the <i>Celine</i> residency show, and the cancellation of her <a href="/wiki/Asia_Tour" title="Asia Tour">Asia Tour</a>, due to the worsening of her husband's health after he underwent the removal of a cancerous tumor in December 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:278px;max-width:278px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:92px;max-width:92px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barbra_streisand.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1637" data-file-width="1090" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Barbra_streisand.jpg/90px-Barbra_streisand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Barbra_streisand.jpg/135px-Barbra_streisand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Barbra_streisand.jpg/180px-Barbra_streisand.jpg 2x" width="90"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bee_Gees_1992.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="566" data-file-width="756" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Bee_Gees_1992.JPG/180px-Bee_Gees_1992.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Bee_Gees_1992.JPG/270px-Bee_Gees_1992.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Bee_Gees_1992.JPG/360px-Bee_Gees_1992.JPG 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Dion was able to collaborate with Barbra Streisand (left) and the Bee Gees (right), both cited as great influences in her recording career.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h3>
<p>Dion cites idols as varied as <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha Franklin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Aznavour" title="Charles Aznavour">Charles Aznavour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carole_King" title="Carole King">Carole King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anne_Murray" title="Anne Murray">Anne Murray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbra_Streisand" title="Barbra Streisand">Barbra Streisand</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bee_Gees" title="Bee Gees">Bee Gees</a>, all of whom she would eventually collaborate with.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion has also stated that she grew up listening to artists such as <a href="/wiki/Janis_Joplin" title="Janis Joplin">Janis Joplin</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doobie_Brothers" title="Doobie Brothers">Doobie Brothers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Creedence_Clearwater_Revival" title="Creedence Clearwater Revival">Creedence Clearwater Revival</a>, but never got the chance to sing their genre of music. She has also shown appreciation for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edith_Piaf" title="Edith Piaf">Edith Piaf</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Elton_John" title="Sir Elton John">Sir Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">Tina Turner</a> and many 1960s, 1970s and 1980s soul singers such as <a href="/wiki/Etta_James" title="Etta James">Etta James</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Flack" title="Roberta Flack">Roberta Flack</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patti_Labelle" title="Patti Labelle">Patti Labelle</a>. Among her peers, she has expressed admiration for fellow vocalist <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>, whom she had often been compared to.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup> Her music has been influenced by numerous genres, including pop, rock, <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a>, and her lyrics focus on themes of poverty, world hunger, and spirituality, with an emphasis on love and romance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated23_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated23-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> After the birth of her first child, her work increasingly focused on maternal love.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celebr_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-celebr-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span></h3>
<p>Dion has faced considerable criticism from critics, who state that her music often retreats behind pop and soul conventions, and is marked by excessive sentimentality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Enc_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-Enc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated24_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated24-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Keith Harris of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine, "[Dion's] sentimentality is bombastic and defiant rather than demure and retiring....[she] stands at the end of the chain of drastic devolution that goes Aretha-Whitney-Mariah. Far from being an aberration, Dion actually stands as a symbol of a certain kind of pop sensibility—bigger is better, too much is never enough, and the riper the emotion the more true."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion's francophone releases, by contrast, tend to be deeper and more varied than her English releases, and consequently have achieved more credibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated21_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated21-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbcc_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbcc-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Critics have stated that Dion's involvement in the production aspect of her music is fundamentally lacking, which results in her work being overproduced<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbcc_209-1"><a href="#cite_note-cbcc-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> and impersonal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated21_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated21-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> However, coming from a family in which all of her siblings were musicians, she dabbled in learning how to play instruments like piano and guitar, and practiced with a <a href="/wiki/Fender_Stratocaster" title="Fender Stratocaster">Fender Stratocaster</a> during the recording sessions of her album, <i>Falling into You</i>. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> Although rare, Dion has contributed to the writing of a handful of her English and French songs, as well as writing a few songs for other artists such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marc_Dupre" title="Marc Dupre">Marc Dupre</a>. Additionally, as her career progressed, she found herself taking charge in the production of her albums. On her first English album, which she recorded before she had a firm command of the English language, she expressed disapproval, which could have been avoided if she had assumed more creative input.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated21_45-4"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated21-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> By the time she released her second English album <i><a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion_(album)" title="Celine Dion (album)">Celine Dion</a></i>, she had assumed more control of the production and recording process, hoping to dispel earlier criticisms. She stated, "On the second album I said, 'Well, I have the choice to be afraid one more time and not be 100% happy, or not be afraid and be part of this album.' This is my album."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated21_45-5"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated21-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Besides her contributions to some of her early French albums, Dion wrote a few of the songs on <i><a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Talk_About_Love" title="Let's Talk About Love">Let's Talk About Love</a></i> (1997) and <i><a href="/wiki/These_Are_Special_Times" title="These Are Special Times">These Are Special Times</a></i> (1998).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-evous.fr_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-evous.fr-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Dion is often the subject of media ridicule<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> and parody, and is frequently impersonated on shows like <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MADtv" title="MADtv">MADtv</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/South_Park" title="South Park">South Park</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Farce" title="Royal Canadian Air Farce">Royal Canadian Air Farce</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/This_Hour_Has_22_Minutes" title="This Hour Has 22 Minutes">This Hour Has 22 Minutes</a></i> for her strong accent and on-stage gesticulations. However, Dion has stated that she is unaffected by the comments, and is flattered that people take the time to impersonate her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vh1_105-2"><a href="#cite_note-vh1-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> She even invited <a href="/wiki/Ana_Gasteyer" title="Ana Gasteyer">Ana Gasteyer</a>, who parodied her on <i>SNL</i>, to appear on stage during one of her performances in New York. While she is rarely politically outspoken, in 2005 following the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> disaster, Dion appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/Larry_King_Live" title="Larry King Live">Larry King Live</a></i> and tearfully criticized the <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">U.S. government</a>'s slow response in aiding the victims of the hurricane: "There's people still there waiting to be rescued. To me that is not acceptable...How can it be so easy to send planes in another country to kill everybody in a second and destroy lives. We need to serve our country."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> After her interview, she stated, "When I do interviews with <a href="/wiki/Larry_King" title="Larry King">Larry King</a> or the big TV shows like that, they put you on the spot, which is very difficult. I do have an opinion, but I'm a singer. I'm not a politician."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice_and_timbre">Voice and timbre</span></h3>
<p>Dion is often regarded as one of pop music's most influential voices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Enc_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-Enc-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated21_45-6"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated21-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Linda Lister in <i>Divafication: The Deification of Modern Female Pop Stars</i>, she has been described as a reigning "<a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Queen of Pop</a>" for her influence over the record industry during the 1990s, alongside other female entertainers, including <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diva_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-diva-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> In a countdown of the "22 Greatest Voices in Music" by <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender Magazine</a></i> and MTV, she placed ninth (sixth for a female), and she was also placed fourth in <i>Cove</i> magazine's list of "The 100 Outstanding Pop Vocalists."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cove_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-cove-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtv22ist_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtv22ist-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion is often compared to Mariah Carey and Whitney Houston for her vocal style and to her idol, <a href="/wiki/Barbra_Streisand" title="Barbra Streisand">Barbra Streisand</a>, for her voice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to various sources, Dion possesses a five-octave <a href="/wiki/Vocal_range" title="Vocal range">vocal range</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> although arguably fully spanning only a three-octave range, from <a href="/wiki/B_(musical_note)" title="B (musical note)">B2</a> to <a href="/wiki/E_(musical_note)" title="E (musical note)">Eb6</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion once stated that she is a <a href="/wiki/Mezzo-soprano" title="Mezzo-soprano">mezzo-soprano</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cyberpresse.ca_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cyberpresse.ca-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> However, attempts to adapt classical voice types to other forms of singing have been met with controversy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> Without making a classification, maestro <a href="/wiki/Kent_Nagano" title="Kent Nagano">Kent Nagano</a> remarked, "All you just sang was <a href="/wiki/Soprano" title="Soprano">soprano</a>," after Dion auditioned with two solos from <i><a href="/wiki/Carmen" title="Carmen">Carmen</a>,</i> wanting to know if she could sing opera.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cyberpresse.ca_224-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cyberpresse.ca-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> Her timbre has been described as "thin, slightly nasal"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTIS_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTIS-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> with a "raspy" lower register and "bell glass-like high notes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Dion is often praised for her technical virtuosity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> Jim Santella of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Buffalo_News" title="The Buffalo News">The Buffalo News</a></i> writes "Like an iron fist in a velvet glove, the power of Celine Dion's voice is cloaked in a silky vibrato that betrays the intensity of her vocal commitment."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BuffaloT_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-BuffaloT-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> Jeff Miers, also of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Buffalo_News" title="The Buffalo News">The Buffalo News</a></i>, says of Dion "Her singing voice is absolutely extra-human. She hits notes in full voice, with a controlled vibrato and an incredible conception of pitch, like she's shucking an ear of corn"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BuffaloT2_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-BuffaloT2-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> Stephen Holden of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> states that Dion has "a good-sized arsenal of technical skills. She can deliver tricky melismas, produce expressive vocal catches and sustain long notes without the tiniest wavering of pitch. And as her duets [...] have shown, she is a reliable harmony voice."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTIS_226-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYTIS-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Lib%C3%A9ration" title="Libération">Libération</a></i>, Jean-Jacques Goldman notes that she has "no problem of accuracy or <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Kent_Nagano" title="Kent Nagano">Kent Nagano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maestro" title="Maestro">maestro</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Munich Symphony Orchestra">Munich Symphony Orchestra</a>, Dion is "a musician who has a good ear, a refinement, and a degree of perfection that is enviable."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cyberpresse.ca_224-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cyberpresse.ca-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> Charles Alexander of <i>TIME</i> states, "[Her] voice glides effortlessly from deep whispers to dead-on high notes, a sweet siren that combines force with grace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated18_38-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated18-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In her French repertoire, Dion adorns her vocals with more nuances and expressiveness, with the emotional intensity being "more tender and intimate."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denise_Bombardier_2009.2C_page_179_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-Denise_Bombardier_2009.2C_page_179-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, Luc Plamondon, a French singer-songwriter who has worked closely with Dion claims that there are three chanteuses (stylistically) that Dion uses: the Québécois, the French, and the American.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denise_Bombardier_2009.2C_page_179_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-Denise_Bombardier_2009.2C_page_179-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> Her self-titled album was promoted with the slogan "Remember the name because you'll never forget the voice."</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Celine_Dion" title="List of awards and nominations received by Celine Dion">List of awards and nominations received by Celine Dion</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Celine_Dion_both_walk_of_fame_stars.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1998" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Celine_Dion_both_walk_of_fame_stars.jpg/220px-Celine_Dion_both_walk_of_fame_stars.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Celine_Dion_both_walk_of_fame_stars.jpg/330px-Celine_Dion_both_walk_of_fame_stars.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Celine_Dion_both_walk_of_fame_stars.jpg/440px-Celine_Dion_both_walk_of_fame_stars.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Celine_Dion_both_walk_of_fame_stars.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Celine Dion's stars on <a href="/wiki/Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame" title="Canada's Walk of Fame">Canada's Walk of Fame</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Celine Dion is regarded as one of pop music's most influential voices. <a href="/wiki/Linda_Lister" title="Linda Lister">Linda Lister</a> describes Dion as a reigning <i>Queen of Pop</i> for her influence over the record industry during the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> Her music and vocal style, alongside that of Mariah Carey and Whitney Houston, have been said to shape how the bulk of modern female pop vocalists sing. These three singers have been widely credited with reviving the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_ballad" title="Power ballad">power ballad</a>, and in doing so reshaping the adult contemporary genre, making it one of the most popular genres of the 1990s and early 2000s. According to producer, musician, and former <a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a> judge <a href="/wiki/Randy_Jackson" title="Randy Jackson">Randy Jackson</a>, Celine Dion, Mariah Carey and Whitney Houston are the voices of the modern era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> Cultural critic Carl Wilson notes that Dion's "fame and influence is also renewed and expressed regularly these days by American Idol, the largest mass musical phenomenon of the past decade, where Celine's stood solidly in its pantheon of singers for young people to emulate".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup> Many contestants on the countless televised talent competitions that have risen at the turn of the millennium often emulate Dion, Houston and Carey and cite them as idols.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Many artists have either mentioned Dion as a major influence or as one of their favorite singers including: <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rita_Ora" title="Rita Ora">Rita Ora</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frank_Ocean" title="Frank Ocean">Frank Ocean</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Josh_Groban" title="Josh Groban">Josh Groban</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grobanarchives.com_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-grobanarchives.com-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Delta_Goodrem" title="Delta Goodrem">Delta Goodrem</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jordin_Sparks" title="Jordin Sparks">Jordin Sparks</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charice" title="Charice">Charice</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leona_Lewis" title="Leona Lewis">Leona Lewis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jessie_J" title="Jessie J">Jessie J</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/JoJo_(singer)" title="JoJo (singer)">Jojo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lea_Michele" title="Lea Michele">Lea Michele</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2015)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Hudson" title="Jennifer Hudson">Jennifer Hudson</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Grande" title="Ariana Grande">Ariana Grande</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Regine_Velasquez" title="Regine Velasquez">Regine Velasquez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vanessa_Hudgens" title="Vanessa Hudgens">Vanessa Hudgens</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Canadian_Tenors" title="The Canadian Tenors">The Canadian Tenors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faith_Hill" title="Faith Hill">Faith Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sevyn_Streeter" title="Sevyn Streeter">Sevyn Streeter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Clarkson" title="Kelly Clarkson">Kelly Clarkson</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Helena_Paparizou" title="Helena Paparizou">Helena Paparizou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lara_Fabian" title="Lara Fabian">Lara Fabian</a>, among many others. In the liner notes of Lara Fabian's album <a href="/wiki/Toutes_les_femmes_en_moi" title="Toutes les femmes en moi">Toutes les femmes en moi</a>, Fabian expressed how she had idolized Dion since her adolescence, even writing: "I would follow note by note your musicality, your passion, sung like only your voice can give colors to the harmony." Country singer <a href="/wiki/Martina_McBride" title="Martina McBride">Martina McBride</a> is widely heralded by the press as the <i>Celine Dion of Country music</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Numerous artists have also praised Dion's voice, singing ability or expressed an interest in working with her including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Placido_Domingo" title="Placido Domingo">Placido Domingo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Santana" title="Carlos Santana">Carlos Santana</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/One_Republic" title="One Republic">One Republic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sharon_Osbourne" title="Sharon Osbourne">Sharon Osbourne</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Scherzinger" title="Nicole Scherzinger">Nicole Scherzinger</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ne-Yo" title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carole_King" title="Carole King">Carole King</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barbra_Streisand" title="Barbra Streisand">Barbra Streisand</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Luciano_Pavarotti" title="Luciano Pavarotti">Luciano Pavarotti</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bee_Gees" title="Bee Gees">Bee Gees</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youtube.com_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-youtube.com-268"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_George_Martin" title="Sir George Martin">Sir George Martin</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youtube.com_268-1"><a href="#cite_note-youtube.com-268"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Goldman" title="Jean-Jacques Goldman">Jean-Jacques Goldman</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a> "Celine has such a beautiful, mesmerizing voice. She is so talented. I think we could create something that is a classic like she is already." Josh Groban remarked "She's a powerhouse. In this day and age, when more and more studio-produced, tiny-tiny voices are being rewarded... she has this extraordinary instrument.".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grobanarchives.com_242-1"><a href="#cite_note-grobanarchives.com-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup> "Celine is the best singer by far of her generation" according to <a href="/wiki/Diane_Warren" title="Diane Warren">Diane Warren</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup> an opinion shared by <a href="/wiki/Quincy_Jones" title="Quincy Jones">Quincy Jones</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Mottola" title="Tommy Mottola">Tommy Mottola</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Foster" title="David Foster">David Foster</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup> Moreover, <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain" title="Shania Twain">Shania Twain</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a> have praised Celine Dion's dynamic stage presence with Jennifer Lopez commenting on American Idol: "Celine gets on stage, she owns the stage, she runs all over that stage, she stops that stage."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On a cultural level, Dion is credited for introducing francophone music to many non-francophone countries around the globe. Her albums <i><a href="/wiki/D%27eux" title="D'eux">D'eux</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/S%27il_suffisait_d%27aimer" title="S'il suffisait d'aimer">S'il suffisait d'aimer</a></i> remain the best selling francophone albums in history gaining unprecedented success in non-Francophone markets such as the United Kingdom, Poland, Netherlands, Portugal, Greece, Austria, Japan and New Zealand. According to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RFI_Musique" title="RFI Musique">RFI Musique</a>, Celine "has done her bit for French music over the years, assuring the success of French songs which would probably never have got beyond Francophone borders without her... Without Celine French record sales would be dramatically lower!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008 Dion received the Legion of Honour from <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> further proving her cultural impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup> Sarkozy praised Celine and stated: "France thanks you because your talent and success have contributed to the influence of the French language outside our borders".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Dion is also credited for both revitalizing and revolutionizing the entertainment scene in Las Vegas with the gargantuan successes of her residencies there. She managed to re-popularize the Las Vegas "residency" as a desirable way for top artists to essentially tour in place, letting their fans come to them. Over the years, fellow established icons such as <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bette_Midler" title="Bette Midler">Bette Midler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart" title="Rod Stewart">Rod Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain" title="Shania Twain">Shania Twain</a> followed suit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span>[</span>280<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Gary Bongiovanni, president and editor-in-chief of <a href="/wiki/Pollstar" title="Pollstar">Pollstar</a> "Celine redefined what artists can do in Las Vegas, helping to make it arguably the busiest entertainment city in the world."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup> By 2013, even the much-younger pop star <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> had announced a Vegas residency, further cementing the extent of Dion's influence on the city as an entertainment capital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2015)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Kurt Melien, vice president of entertainment at Caesar's Palace stated "Celine was a pioneer without question..Twenty years ago, we couldn't have got someone the stature of Britney Spears to appear in Vegas. Stars likes her would never have considered it if Celine hadn't paved the way. She changed the face of modern Vegas."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283"><span>[</span>283<span>]</span></a></sup> Regarding her financial impact on Las Vegas, Stephen Brown, director of the Centre for Business and Economic Research in Las Vegas, commented "People will come to the city just for her and they will spend money and as a consequence, she has an outsized impact on the economy", then adding "Bigger than Elvis, Sinatra and Liberace put together? Definitely.". Estimations indicate that Dion's show will create up to 7,000 indirect jobs and around $114 million worth of new economic activity in each of the three years for which she has been contracted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284"><span>[</span>284<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1999, Dion received a star on <a href="/wiki/Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame" title="Canada's Walk of Fame">Canada's Walk of Fame</a> and also a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> in January 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285"><span>[</span>285<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286"><span>[</span>286<span>]</span></a></sup> She dedicated her star to her father, who died the month prior. In 2007, Dion was ranked by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> as the 5th richest woman in entertainment with an estimated net worth of US$250 million, though the ranking omitted non-working or retired celebrities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287"><span>[</span>287<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289"><span>[</span>289<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2008, she received an honorary doctorate in music from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Laval" title="Université Laval">Université Laval</a> in Quebec City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2010, Dion was named a <a href="/wiki/FAO_Goodwill_Ambassador" title="FAO Goodwill Ambassador">Goodwill Ambassador</a>, a program created by the UN in 1999, sharing this accolade with Oscar-winner <a href="/wiki/Susan_Sarandon" title="Susan Sarandon">Susan Sarandon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion also received several <a href="/wiki/State_decoration" title="State decoration">state decorations</a>. She was given France's highest award, the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Légion d'honneur</a>, by <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> in May 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292"><span>[</span>292<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup> On 26 July 2013, Dion was awarded with the Companion of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Canada" title="Order of Canada">Order of Canada</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a> and the investiture ceremony was held at <a href="/wiki/Citadelle_of_Quebec" title="Citadelle of Quebec">Citadelle of Quebec</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294"><span>[</span>294<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_activities">Other activities</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_endeavors">Business endeavors</span></h3>
<p>Les Productions Feeling Inc., also known as Feeling Inc. or just Feeling, is an artist management company based in Laval, Québec, Canada and owned by Dion and her husband and manager, Rene Angelil. Dion is also founder of Nickels Restaurant food chain. Dion and her husband also own Le Mirage Golf Club and Schwartz's Restaurant. In association with Andre Agassi, Steffi Graf and Shaquille O'Neal she opened a popular night club called <i>Pure</i>, located at Caesars Palace.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Dion became an entrepreneur with the establishment of her <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchise</a> restaurant, <i><a href="/wiki/Nickels_Grill_%26_Bar" title="Nickels Grill &amp; Bar">Nickels</a></i> in 1990. She has since divested her interests in the chain and is no longer affiliated with <i>Nickels</i>, as of 1997.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2003, Dion signed a deal with <a href="/wiki/Coty,_Inc." title="Coty, Inc.">Coty, Inc.</a> to release <i><a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion_Parfums" title="Celine Dion Parfums">Celine Dion Parfums</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davis_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davis-295"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup> Her latest fragrance, <i>Signature</i>, was released in September 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celinedion1_185-1"><a href="#cite_note-celinedion1-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> with an advertising campaign by New York agency Kraftworks NYC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296"><span>[</span>296<span>]</span></a></sup> Since its inception, <i>Celine Dion Parfums</i> has grossed over $850 million in retail sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brilliance_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-brilliance-297"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298"><span>[</span>298<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2004, <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a> hired Dion as part of their promotional campaign to unveil new service products and an updated <a href="/wiki/Livery" title="Livery">livery</a>. "<a href="/wiki/You_and_I_(Celine_Dion_song)" title="You and I (Celine Dion song)">You and I</a>", the theme song sung by Dion, was written by advertising executives working for Air Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span></h3>
<p>Dion has actively supported many charity organizations, worldwide. She has promoted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Cystic_Fibrosis_Foundation" title="Canadian Cystic Fibrosis Foundation">Canadian Cystic Fibrosis Foundation</a> (CCFF) since 1982, and became the foundation's National Celebrity Patron in 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300"><span>[</span>300<span>]</span></a></sup> She has an emotional attachment to the foundation; her niece Karine succumbed to the disease at the age of sixteen, in Dion's arms. In 2003, she joined a number of other celebrities, athletes, and politicians, including <a href="/wiki/Josh_Groban" title="Josh Groban">Josh Groban</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yolanda_Adams" title="Yolanda Adams">Yolanda Adams</a> to support "World Children's Day", a global fundraising effort sponsored by <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a>. The effort raised money from more than 100 nations and benefited orphanages and children's health organizations. In addition, Dion has been a major supporter of the <a href="/wiki/Tony_Martell" title="Tony Martell">T.J. Martell Foundation</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diana_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana Princess of Wales">Diana Princess of Wales</a> Memorial Fund, and many health and educational campaigns. During the aftermath of Hurricane Katrina, Dion donated $1 million to the victims of the storm, and held a fund-raising event for the victims of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Asian_Tsunami" title="2004 Asian Tsunami">2004 Asian Tsunami</a>, which subsequently raised more than $1 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/2008_Sichuan_earthquake" title="2008 Sichuan earthquake">2008 Sichuan earthquake</a>, Dion donated $100,000 to China Children &amp; Teenagers' Fund and sent a letter showing her consolation and support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302"><span>[</span>302<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 2004, she is involved, alongside husband René Angelil, with the Québec gay community by supporting the publication of health and HIV prevention materials in <i>Gay Globe Magazine</i>, owned by journalist Roger-Luc Chayer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303"><span>[</span>303<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A9line_Dion_Ren%C3%A9_Angelil_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="505" data-file-width="800" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/C%C3%A9line_Dion_Ren%C3%A9_Angelil_2012.jpg/220px-C%C3%A9line_Dion_Ren%C3%A9_Angelil_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/C%C3%A9line_Dion_Ren%C3%A9_Angelil_2012.jpg/330px-C%C3%A9line_Dion_Ren%C3%A9_Angelil_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/C%C3%A9line_Dion_Ren%C3%A9_Angelil_2012.jpg/440px-C%C3%A9line_Dion_Ren%C3%A9_Angelil_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A9line_Dion_Ren%C3%A9_Angelil_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dion and husband <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Ang%C3%A9lil" title="René Angélil">René Angélil</a> in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Dion resides in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas, Nevada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304"><span>[</span>304<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion first met her husband and manager, <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Ang%C3%A9lil" title="René Angélil">René Angélil</a> in 1980, when she was 12 and he was 38, after she and her mother sent him a demo tape of a song they had written.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They began a relationship in 1987, and became engaged in 1991. They married on 17 December 1994, at <a href="/wiki/Notre-Dame_Basilica_(Montreal)" title="Notre-Dame Basilica (Montreal)">Notre-Dame Basilica</a> in Montreal, Quebec. On 5 January 2000, Dion and Angelil renewed their wedding vows in Las Vegas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In May 2000, Dion had two small operations at a fertility clinic in New York to improve her chances of conceiving, after deciding to use <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In-vitro_fertilisation" title="In-vitro fertilisation">in-vitro fertilisation</a> due to years of failed attempts to conceive. Their first son, René-Charles Angelil, was born on 25 January 2001. In May 2010, Angelil announced that Dion was 14 weeks pregnant with twins after a sixth treatment of in-vitro fertilisation. On Saturday, 23 October 2010, at 11:11 and 11:12 am respectively, at <a href="/wiki/St._Mary_Medical_Center_(Long_Beach)" title="St. Mary Medical Center (Long Beach)">St. Mary's Medical Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">West Palm Beach, Florida</a>, Dion, by <a href="/wiki/Caesarean_section" title="Caesarean section">Caesarean section</a>, gave birth to healthy fraternal twins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305"><span>[</span>305<span>]</span></a></sup> The twins were named Eddy, after Dion's favorite Algerian songwriter <a href="/wiki/Eddy_Marnay" title="Eddy Marnay">Eddy Marnay</a> who also produced Dion's first five albums, and Nelson, after former South African President <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306"><span>[</span>306<span>]</span></a></sup> Dion appeared with her newborn sons on the cover of 9 December 2010 issue of the Canadian edition of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hello!" title="Hello!">Hello!</a></i> magazine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307"><span>[</span>307<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
